    A non-exhaustive list of these operations,\n1327:     which can be computed by `einsum`, is shown below along with examples:\n1328: \n1329:     * Trace of an array, :py:func:`numpy.trace`.\n1330:     * Return a diagonal, :py:func:`numpy.diag`.\n1331:     * Array axis summations, :py:func:`numpy.sum`.\n1332:     * Transpositions and permutations, :py:func:`numpy.transpose`.\n1333: ","endLine":1333,"startLine":1326},{"content":"1377:     NumPy-style broadcasting is done by adding an ellipsis\n1378:     to the left of each term, like ``np.einsum('...ii->...i', a)``.\n1379:     ``np.einsum('...i->...', a)`` is like\n1380:     :py:func:`np.sum(a, axis=-1) <numpy.sum>` for array ``a`` of any shape.\n1381:     To take the trace along the first and last axes,\n1382:     you can do ``np.einsum('i...i', a)``, or to do a matrix-matrix\n1383:     product with the left-most indices instead of rightmost, one can do\n1384:     ``np.einsum('ij...,jk...->ik...', a, b)``.\n1385: \n1386:     When there is only one operand, no axes are summed, and no output\n1387:     parameter is provided, a view into the operand is returned instead\n1388:     of a new array. general limited by directly adding each number\n2376:     individually to the result causing rounding errors in every step.\n2377:     However, often numpy will use a  numerically better approach (partial\n2378:     pairwise summation) leading to improved precision in many use-cases.\n2379:     This improved precision is always provided when no ``axis`` is given.\n2380:     When ``axis`` is given, it will depend on which axis is summed.\n2381:     Technically, to provide the best speed possible, the improved precision\n2382:     is only used when the summation is along the fast axis in memory.\n2383:     Note that the exact precision may vary depending on other parameters.\n2384:     In contrast to NumPy, Python's ``math.fsum`` function uses a slower but\n2385:     more precise approach to summation.\n2386:     Especially when summing a large number of lower precision floating point\n2387:     numbers, such as ``float32``, numerical errors can become significant.\n2388:     In such cases it can be advisable to use `dtype=np.float64` to use a higher\n2389:     precision for the output.\n2390: \n2391:     Examples\n2392:     --------\n2393:     >>> import numpy as np\n2394:     >>> np.sum([0.5, 1.5])\n2395:     2.0\n2396:     >>> np.sum([0.5, 0.7, 0.2, 1.5], dtype=np.int32)\n2397:     np.int32(1)\n2398:     >>> np.sum([[0, 1], [0, 5]])\n2399:     6\n2400:     >>> np.sum([[0, 1], [0, 5]], axis=0)\n2401: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/numpy--a639fbf5@a639fbf5d2a4fb789967124d16f503f57bd5958b/-/blob/numpy/_core/fromnumeric.py%3FL2298-2400"}}}
